U.S., British, and French Ambassadors to Meet with Molotov Today, Presenting a Joint New Note, Hoping to Facilitate Four-Power Negotiations on the German Question

[United Press, London, 28th] U.S. Ambassador to the Soviet Union, Smith, has departed for Moscow by special plane this evening and is expected to arrive in Moscow on the 29th. Smith's special plane stopped briefly in Berlin at midnight.

Another dispatch: Roberts, the private secretary to British Foreign Secretary Bevin, left London on the 28th for Moscow, together with representatives from the U.S. and France, to deliver the Western response to the Kremlin. Roberts, who was originally the British Minister to the Soviet Union, will fly to Berlin on the same plane as General Robertson, the British military commander in Germany, and then fly to Moscow with U.S. Ambassador to the Soviet Union, General Smith.

[United Press, London, 28th] According to authoritative sources, the U.S., French, and British ambassadors to the Soviet Union will inform Soviet Foreign Minister Molotov in Moscow on the 29th of the decision made at the London Conference regarding relations with the Soviet Union. They will place the biggest bet since the end of the war, which could be for peace or war, but not necessarily immediate peace or immediate war. However, they also said that this new negotiation with the Soviet Union and the Soviet Union's response could be a turning point for the situation to improve or worsen. This oral note was handled with extreme caution and long preparation beforehand. The various departments of the U.S. government have never paid so much attention to diplomatic action before. It is generally expected that the U.S., British, and French ambassadors will frankly tell Molotov that their governments are prepared to begin negotiations with the Soviet Union on the German question as soon as the Berlin blockade is lifted. This negotiation does not mean that a four-power foreign ministers' conference will be convened immediately, as the preparatory work for a four-power foreign ministers' conference will take a long time. It is generally expected that the Western powers will first suggest negotiations through normal diplomatic channels and the Allied Control Council for Germany.

[United Press, London, 28th] Authoritative sources said that Smith will make oral representations to Molotov on behalf of the U.S., Britain, and France, pointing out that the Berlin blockade violates Article 2 of the United Nations Charter, which states that "Members of the United Nations shall settle their international disputes by peaceful means in such a manner that international peace and security, and justice, are not endangered." This is the decision reached at the London Conference of the U.S., Britain, and France. There is no doubt that the Western powers have reached an agreement and may finally agree to convene a four-power conference or refer the Berlin issue to the United Nations, but at this stage, the Western powers have agreed to delay any action that could lead to the reopening of the four-power foreign ministers' conference or an appeal to the United Nations.

[This newspaper] Geneva, 28th broadcast: Washington dispatch: Marshall told reporters that the United States has reached an agreement with Britain and France on the Berlin issue but refused to disclose the contents of this agreement. At the same time, he was unwilling to confirm or deny whether the three governments had instructed their ambassadors to the Soviet Union to discuss the Berlin situation directly with Molotov.

Republicans Attempt to Attack Truman, Decide to Adopt Delaying Tactics, Plan to Request Congress to Adjourn, Making the Plan Fail

[United Press, Washington, 27th] The special session of the U.S. Congress convened by President Truman to establish anti-inflation legislation was attacked by Truman on the 27th, as Republican leaders accused Truman's plan of having political purposes and launched an offensive to quickly adjourn the meeting. In fact, they will make Truman's hopes for all his demands to vanish. After discussing Truman's plan by telephone with the Republican presidential candidate Dewey, the Republican leaders agreed to consider Truman's plan. But they made it clear that they did not intend to turn any of these plans into legislation and said that they planned to stop the meeting and return home in two weeks.

In addition, they will put the anti-poll tax bill passed by the House of Representatives on the first item of discussion on the Senate agenda, thus setting up a huge obstacle in the way of any action. At the same time, Democratic Senator Johnston (South Carolina) has prepared to propose an adjournment, and he is the leader of the Democratic rebellious senators in the eleven southern states who oppose Truman's demands for racial rights. After the Republican leaders held a strategy meeting, they replied with a policy declaration of more than a thousand words, denouncing the president's convening of the special conference as a political means to seek re-election as president. They accused the Democratic government of being responsible for the current high prices and stated that they were willing to hand over the matter to the people of the whole country to decide in the November election. Truman had previously told the hostile Congress that Congress must stop inflation, otherwise, it would bear the brunt of the unpopular tragedy. He demanded the rapid passage of the collection of excessive profit tax, the restriction of wages and prices, the power to assign the distribution system, and other measures to "stop the rising prices." He also demanded that action be taken on the construction of housing programs now and not next year, and listed other major domestic issues.

[United Press, Washington, 27th] The words of Taft, chairman of the Senate Joint Party Policy Committee, can represent the Republican response. He said, "Considering the president's entire plan will take six months," and "these three points only emphasize the following facts, that is, the convening of the special parliament obviously has a political purpose."

Truman's Proposal, Unions Express Approval

[United Press, Washington, 27th] Unions today expressed their approval of President Truman's message to Congress. Spokespersons for the Industrial Confederation and the Labor Federation said that the president's proposal included most of the laws supported by their 1,300 members. However, they were not very enthusiastic about the wage control proposal. The Industrial Confederation made it clear that they opposed such control, claiming that careful study of inflation proved that wages were not the cause. Union spokespersons unanimously believed that the special meeting would allow voters to judge the performance of members in the November election.

New Currency Exchange in the Soviet Occupation Zone, Serious Riots Occurred Yesterday

[This newspaper] London, 28th broadcast, Berlin dispatch: In the Soviet occupation zone of Berlin, riots have broken out because tens of thousands of people are crowding in front of banks to exchange new currency. After the riots occurred, the Soviet Union immediately blamed the non-Communist Berlin City Government, accusing it of failing to set up enough exchange offices in advance, so that the people who exchanged new currencies could avoid crowding, thereby preventing the occurrence of riots. But officials of the U.S. military government said that the Berlin City Government was a "scapegoat." At the same time, newspapers in the four occupation zones openly criticized the Soviet Union for this move, aiming to squeeze the wealth of the Germans.

United Nations Small Assembly Decides to Establish an International Mediation Commissioner Group, This Proposal is Jointly Proposed by the United States and China

[United States Information Service, Lake Success, 27th] The United Nations Interim Committee, that is, the "Small General Assembly," continued to discuss the report of the Subcommittee on the Peaceful Settlement of Disputes today. The "Small General Assembly" approved the main construction of the Subcommittee on Monday. The approved proposals advocate the establishment of an International Mediation Commissioner Group, stipulate that the Chairman of the United Nations General Assembly and the members of the Security Council shall assume new mediation responsibilities, and enable the Interim Committee to continue its study plan on the peaceful settlement of disputes. The proposal to establish the International Mediation Commissioner Group was jointly proposed by the United States and China to make mediation experts available to countries in dispute (United Nations member states or non-member states). According to this plan, each country will be invited to propose one to five representatives, serving a five-year term, and countries involved in disputes or United Nations agencies may select mediation commissioners from this group of experts.

Dewey's Brain Trust

— Translated by Zhang Yunshi —

The other figures may not be well known throughout the United States, but they have hopes of forming a cabinet with Dewey. The expected situation is as follows:

Lockwood, one of Dewey's brain trusts, is 46 years old this year. He is Dewey's administrative advisor and may be appointed as the chief secretary of the White House if the Republican Party is elected. He has the power to decide who can and cannot see Dewey. Lockwood is a burly and amiable figure who used to practice law. He joined the Dewey brain trust in 1935 when he prosecuted New York gangsters.

Hedge, a former reporter for "The New York Times," is 39 years old. Unlike O'Reilly under the Roosevelt administration and Ross under the Truman administration, he has no experience as a Washington reporter. He has a good relationship with Dewey.

Burton, 40, is the current budget director of Governor Dewey. He may be appointed as the director of the US Budget Bureau when Dewey is president. Chapman, 44 this year, first took office as the New York Tax Commissioner in 1946. He is one of Dewey's financial advisors. Strauss, 59 this year, is a planning expert and may naturally be assigned a corresponding task.

The above are the internal figures of Dewey. For the remaining departments, he needs to find people from the Republican family.

The position of Secretary of Defense may be held by Senator Martin from Pennsylvania, 68 years old. The next most promising candidate is Senator Cain from Washington.

The position of Secretary of Agriculture may be held by Hopper, 55 years old this year, from Kansas, currently chairman of the Agricultural Committee. The next most promising candidate is Mayo. He is the president of Cornell University and formerly served as the administrator of the agricultural trust loan organization. Ferguson, a senator from Michigan, may be the Attorney General.

Winnemas, 47 years old this year, is a senator from Oregon. He may be appointed as the Secretary of the Interior after Dewey is elected. Milligan, 57 years old this year, is a senator from Carolina. Although he supported Taft before the Philadelphia Convention, he also has hopes of being appointed as the Secretary of the Interior or other important positions. However, his hope of remaining in the Senate is also very high.

Stetson, 41 years old this year, failed in the presidential candidate election, but his call to join the Dewey administration is also very high.

Hoffman is 57 years old this year. He used to run an automobile business and is currently the director of the European Aid Administration. He may be appointed as the Secretary of Commerce after Dewey becomes president, but he may also remain as the director of the European Aid Administration if he is willing to do so.

Milton Eisenhower, 49 years old this year, is the brother of Marshal Eisenhower and the current president of Kansas State College. He may be appointed as the Secretary of Education or the Secretary of Health.

After Dewey is elected president, the main figures in the White House may also become a completely New York-dominated administration. Now, regardless of the situation after Dewey takes office, in short, if Dewey is elected as the next president, under the circumstances of new people and new policies, he may do a good job. (End) (Translated from the July issue of American World News)

Executive Yuan Supports Shanghai's Finances, One-Time Subsidy of 1.4 Trillion, Budget Review Committee Report Believes It Should Not Rely on the Central Government

[Our Dispatch from Nanjing, 28th] Regarding Shanghai's financial difficulties and the proposal to request subsidies from the central government, after repeated trips by Tian Yong, Director of the Shanghai Municipal Finance Bureau, the case was submitted for discussion at the Executive Yuan meeting on the 28th and it was resolved to grant a one-time subsidy of 1.4 trillion yuan. It has been learned that the Shanghai Municipal Government's telegram will include an additional half-month's living allowance for civil servants and teachers for June, which must be settled according to the index for that month, and the living allowance to be paid this month has reached 1.4 trillion yuan, and the index settlement will be at least 600 billion yuan or more. In addition, other temporary expenses for office, economic construction, and health, based on low estimates, require about 400 billion yuan, totaling 2.4 trillion yuan. On the income side, there is only about 1 trillion yuan, so the shortfall for this month alone will reach 1.4 trillion yuan. In addition to requesting approval for subsidies for the monthly revenue and expenditure shortfalls in the second half of this year, it is also requested that the 1.4 trillion yuan shortfall for July be allocated first by emergency order before the 20th of this month, and then supplemented later. After receiving the telegram, the Executive Yuan handed it over to the Budget Review Committee for review, and on the 28th, discussed it based on the review opinions. According to the review report, "Shanghai's industry and commerce are prosperous, and the tax base is relatively wealthy. It should increase revenue through various means and should not rely on central government subsidies. This time, the city government increased the living allowance for employees by half a month in June, and temporary expenditures increased sharply. Tax collection could not adapt, and prices continued to rise, and the difference between revenue and expenditure became even greater. What has been stated is indeed the actual situation. It is proposed to approve a one-time discretionary subsidy for some temporary expenses for economic construction and health, and submit it to the Executive Yuan meeting for decision." After discussion at the Executive Yuan meeting on the 28th, it was decided to grant a one-time subsidy of 1.4 trillion yuan based on this report. In addition, Director Tian of the Shanghai Field Bureau returned to Shanghai by overnight train on the 28th.

Norwegian Ship Runs Aground at Wusong Estuary, Towed for Repair, Departure Date Postponed

[Our Dispatch] The Norwegian ship Leitcht (transliteration) of the Norwegian shipping company, which arrived in Shanghai from Europe with a large number of paper and other goods the day before yesterday, arrived at the Wusong estuary at 5 p.m. The shipowner himself took the position of pilot and drove into the port. Unexpectedly, due to inadvertent negligence, it ran aground, the forward hold was punctured, and the river water entered. An urgent telegram was sent to Shanghai to report the incident. Upon receiving the news, the company immediately borrowed the Guoyang steamer from the China Merchants Bureau for rescue. After the Guoyang steamer towed it out of danger, it was towed into the port and berthed at buoy No. 42.44. There was a lot of water in the forward hold. The Guoyang steamer pumped water overnight. Because water was being pumped out on one side, and river water was still entering continuously on the other side, it was impossible to pump it all out. Yesterday, the company prepared to remove the paper in the hold, continue pumping water, and hire divers to repair the leak, and then enter the dock for repairs. This work will take two or three days to complete, and the repairs will also take a considerable amount of time. The original plan was to load cargo and return to Europe at the end of this month, so the export must be postponed.

Number of Poor Exceeds 880,000

Land Administration Bureau Planning to Levy Vacant Land Tax, to Promote Land Use, to Achieve the Goal of Relieving the Housing Shortage

[Our Dispatch] The city's population has recently increased sharply, forming an unprecedentedly serious housing shortage. However, in fact, there are still many vacant lots in the city that have not been used, and are still allowed to be abandoned. Relevant parties are paying close attention to this issue. According to news from the Land Administration Bureau, the bureau is currently planning to levy a vacant land tax in accordance with the resolution of the sixth general meeting of the Municipal Council, and has already drafted a plan. As soon as it is submitted to the municipal government for approval, it can be officially implemented. It is heard that this method is based on the provisions of Article 173 of the Land Law, designating areas and setting a time limit for building houses. If the houses are not built after the time limit, a vacant land tax will be levied, and the tax rate will be three times and ten times the land value tax to be paid. The levy of land value tax is based on the value of the land itself. The vacant land tax is levied on top of the land value tax. The intention of increasing the tax burden on vacant land without any income is to promote the use of land through taxation. It is not uncommon to see cases where major cities in the world have adopted this measure and achieved results.

Mayor Wu will concurrently serve as the chairman of the People's Livelihood Research Association, and I will serve as a standing committee member to assist the chairman in his work. The People's Livelihood Research Association will set up an allocation office, and the position of director will be held by the current chief secretary Lu Guixiang. The original offices will be changed to groups, which will be under the jurisdiction of the office. We will try to maintain both the per capita rice and the poor people's rice so that they are not interrupted."

Resuming Livestock Import Inspection

[Our Dispatch] The city's daily consumption of meat livestock is very large. In order to ensure the meat hygiene of citizens, the Municipal Health Bureau, after a resolution by the municipal conference and the Municipal Council, has resumed livestock import inspection and ordered the diseased animal rendering plant to start running on a set date. In the future, anyone transporting livestock into the city must first apply to the Wusong Maigen Road inspection stations of the plant for inspection and give a certificate to transport them into the urban area. Without a certificate, they will not be allowed to pass. It is now learned that the rendering plant is actively preparing and will be implemented soon.

Chinese Maritime Construction Association Holds First Preparatory Meeting, Du Yuesheng Speaks, Hoping for Early Establishment

[Our Newspaper Report] Twenty-seven units including labor and management of our country's shipping and fishing industries, academic groups, etc., in order to concentrate forces, promote maritime culture, promote shipping construction, maintain navigation marks, and enhance mutual assistance and cooperation, decided to organize the Chinese Maritime Construction Association at the First Navigation Day Conference on the 3rd of this month. Yesterday afternoon at 4 o'clock, the first preparatory meeting was held on the sixth floor of the China Merchants Bureau. Representatives from various groups, including Du Yuesheng, Qian Xinzh, Yang Guanbei, Xu Xueyu, Zhong Shandao, Huang Jiaqiu, Shen Zhongyi, Zhang Shusheng, Yang Ying, and Huang Muzong, Director of the Maritime Administration, and more than fifty others attended. Du Yuesheng was publicly elected as chairman. Mr. Du delivered an opening speech, briefly stating: The first Navigation Day in our country on July 3 this year fully demonstrated the spirit of unity in our shipping industry and also symbolized the infinitely bright future of China's shipping construction. The organization of the Chinese Maritime Construction Association was a resolution unanimously passed at that conference. It is hoped that after today's meeting, preparatory work can be carried out quickly so that the Maritime Construction Association can be established as soon as possible.

Ten Major Work Objectives

After the chairman's speech, the discussion of the draft regulations of the association began. The representatives present spoke enthusiastically and decided on the ten major work objectives of the association: (1) Study nautical academics, (2) Review shipping policies, (3) Promote shipbuilding industry, (4) Advocate shipping insurance, (5) Assist in organizing port affairs, (6) Guide shipping investment, (7) Expand shipping education, (8) Promote fisheries construction, (9) Revise maritime regulations, (10) Enhance unity in the shipping industry.

Regarding membership qualifications, it was stipulated that all maritime affairs, shipping culture, as well as shipping and fishing organizations, can participate. Funding: (1) The foundation will be raised through fundraising. (2) Recurring expenses will be mainly from membership fees and annual membership dues. (3) Business expenses will be mainly from the revenue of various business operations.

Electing Chairman and Vice-Chairman

Organization: A board of directors and supervisors system will be adopted, and for the convenience of promoting work, various research committees will be established, including: (1) Maritime Technology Research Committee, (2) Shipping Management Research Committee, (3) Shipbuilding Engineering Research Committee, (4) Shipping Economics Research Committee, (5) Shipping Insurance Research Committee, (6) Port Construction Research Committee, (7) International Shipping Research Committee, (8) Ship Inspection Research Committee, (9) Maritime Regulations Research Committee, (10) Maritime Education and Culture Research Committee, (11) Labor-Management Cooperation Issues Research Committee, (12) Fisheries Construction Research Committee, (13) Shipping Policy Review Committee, (14) Seafarer Welfare Undertakings Research Committee.

It was also decided that all representatives attending the first preparatory meeting would be preparatory committee members, and Du Yuesheng and Huang Muzong were publicly elected as chairman and vice-chairman respectively. Finally, Xu Xueyu proposed that the official inaugural meeting be held on September 9 of this year, which was unanimously agreed upon and passed. The meeting adjourned at 5:15 PM.

Representatives from various factories in the thermos bottle shell department of the printing industry workers' union requested that wages be paid according to the current index. Shen Da Factory Steam Tank Explosion, Deputy Factory Director Found Guilty

[Our Newspaper Report] At 3:00 PM on June 13, the first factory of Shen Da Rubber Factory experienced an explosion due to excessive heat in the steam tank. The roof caught fire and burned. The police station transferred the case to the District Procuratorate for investigation. The District Procuratorate found that the deputy factory director, Liu Zou, failed to supervise Wang Junshan, the foreman in charge of the steam tank, which was the most dangerous part of the factory, to take extra precautions. He was therefore found to have been seriously negligent and was publicly prosecuted on suspicion of endangering public safety.

Spot Checks on Business Tax Personnel, Must Wear Badges When on Duty

[Our Newspaper Report] The Finance Bureau's spot checks on business tax work have already begun. In order to prevent impersonation and fraud, the bureau specifically stipulates that field personnel must carry badges, duty certificates, and duty slips when on duty. These duty slips are divided into three types: Type A, Special Type, and Type B. Type A and Special Type duty badges are used to check registers and retrieve account books and must be stamped with the Finance Bureau's official seal and the director's personal seal. Type B duty slips are used to investigate situations other than account books. Those issued by the Tax Collection Office should be stamped with the office's seal and the director's personal seal. Shops and residents can verify the above documents when encountering investigators.

Two Defendants Who Damaged Power Plant, Case Submitted to Central Government for Review

Wang Xiaohe, Standing Director of the Shanghai Electric Power Company Industry Union, and worker Wu Chezhen, who were convicted of conspiring to sabotage the power company and sentenced to the death penalty, expressed their dissatisfaction with the verdict and petitioned the Special Court to submit the case file to the Central Government for review. The court replied yesterday, stating that it had submitted the case file to the Central Government for review in accordance with Article 6 of the Special Criminal Court Trial Regulations.

Embezzling and Selling Steel Cables from the Supply Bureau, Inspectors and Others Arrested for Investigation

[Our Newspaper Report] A foreign ship chartered by the Executive Yuan's Materials Supply Bureau transported surplus American military supplies of steel cables from Guam to Shanghai on June 28 of this year. After arriving at the Kaiping Wharf, Chen Shuping and Shao Guozheng, wharf inspectors of the bureau, colluded with Huang Ban and Ge Xingkun to embezzle and sell the steel cables privately, transporting them away in small sampans. Chen and others gave tens of thousands of US dollars to Huang, Ge, and others, and another inspector of the bureau, Guo Dianxun, was given ten US dollars. The case was subsequently discovered, and the bureau sent personnel to thoroughly investigate and found it to be true. Chen, Shao, and others were detained, and a document was prepared and transferred to the District Procuratorate for interrogation.

University Student Refuses to Marry, Fiancée Denies Writing Letter of Repentance, Taken to Police Station Then to Court, Interrogated and Accused of Adultery

[Our Newspaper Report] On June 26 of this year, Peng Zhixing, a native of Huangyan, Zhejiang, and his daughter Peng Chujiao went to the police station to accuse Feng Ji, a student at Great China University, claiming that from November of last year to January 25 of this year, his daughter Peng was raped three times by her fiancé Feng Ji in the Zhongnan, Da Hu, and Da Shanghai hotels. Unexpectedly, after becoming pregnant for five months, Feng Ji refused to marry her and avoided meeting her. They requested that the police station arrest him. Feng was subsequently arrested by the police station at the Dada Wharf. According to Feng's confession: His marriage to Peng Chujiao was arranged by his uncle Wang Mengxia and Zhang Yuhua as matchmakers, and decided by his parents. The engagement took place in his hometown on the sixth day of the fourth lunar month last year. At the time, he was studying in Shanghai and did not know about it beforehand. Later, Peng came to Shanghai to study at the Southeast Medical College. Because she was unfamiliar with the place, he often accompanied her to go out shopping and watch movies. In November of last year, after watching a movie with Peng, it was too late, so they opened a room at the Zhongnan Restaurant and stayed overnight, and thus the relationship occurred. At the time, he discovered that Peng Chujiao was not a virgin, but Peng refused to reveal the truth. Later, in December of last year and January 25 of this year, they secretly met at the Da Hu and Da Shanghai hotels respectively. Through honeyed words, he finally learned that Peng had already had a relationship with Zhu Yao and Zheng Deyi before the engagement. At the time, in order to express her remorse, she personally wrote a letter of repentance and handed it to him. However, he believed that Peng had lost her virginity twice, making it difficult for her to become a lifelong partner, so he refused to marry her. At the same time, he presented the letter of repentance, the original text of which is as follows: "Peng Chujiao is 21 years old this year, a native of Huangyan, Zhejiang. At the age of 16, she studied at the Linhai Private Jiancheng Middle School and had an affair with Zhu Yaojun. At that time, due to emotional impulses, her virginity was broken by Mr. Zhu. At the age of 17, she transferred to the Huangyan County Middle School and met her sister's husband, Mr. Zheng Deyi, and was seduced and had a relationship once. These two events are the greatest shame of my life. But from now on, I will never go down this wrong path again. If similar things happen in the future, then Feng Ji can punish me in any way he wants, and I will never go back on my word. This is my word. Repenter: Peng Chujiao, April 21." Peng resolutely denied writing the letter of repentance. The police station then transferred the case to the District Procuratorate. After interrogation, Feng Ji was formally prosecuted for having sexual relations with a girl under the age of 20 (Peng Chujiao was born on the sixth day of the sixth lunar month, and was not yet 20 years old when the relationship with Feng Ji occurred). The trial will be held in the District Court soon.

[Our Newspaper Report] The Fisheries Relief Material Distribution Meeting hosted by the Post-War Relief and Rehabilitation Administration was held at the YMCA in the Eight Immortals Bridge yesterday. Representatives from the Ministry of Agriculture and Forestry, the Ministry of Social Affairs, the Ministry of Transportation, and the Ministry of Industry and Commerce were also present. The opening ceremony was held in the morning, with an opening speech by Pan Xulun, Acting Chairman of the Post-War Relief and Rehabilitation Administration. Representatives from various ministries also delivered speeches one after another. After the ceremony, they visited the Fisheries Administration Office. The official conference was held in the afternoon. The agenda included reading the origins of the Fisheries Vessel Material Utilization Plan for the seven regions, reporting on relevant resolutions of the plan, the custody committee reporting on the general situation of ship materials, the Fisheries Administration Office reporting on the material custody situation, and discussing the rules of procedure and nominating the organization review panel. The meeting will last for three days. Today is the panel review meeting, and tomorrow will be the general meeting. The meeting will close at 5:00 PM.

The villagers of Sanjiang, for self-defense, organized self-defense teams, but were falsely accused of being "bandit followers." At the beginning of constitutional governance, Longquan used dark forces to arbitrarily kill people, which is a disregard for the law. In order to defend justice, the association will publish the true facts in the hope of gaining sympathy and support from the press and the public.

Asia-Pacific Lightweight Light Bulbs Not Meeting Standards Is Misinformation

It was rumored that the lightweight light bulbs produced by the China Asia-Pacific Electrical Appliance Factory did not meet standards. Hu Xiyuan, the general manager of the factory, recently inquired with Ouyang Lun, the director of the Industry and Commerce Guidance Office, about the source of this rumor. Ouyang replied that he had not heard of the news. Hu then requested that he inquire with the Ministry of Industry and Commerce. The investigation revealed that lightweight light bulbs are manufactured in response to actual needs due to the different voltages of power plants in various regions. Therefore, the news spread outside was due to a misunderstanding.

Sun Pusheng Incident in Jiangyin, Trial Set for the 31st, Witnesses Huang Enrong and Others to Be Interrogated, County Magistrate and Township Head Express Their Opinions, All Advocate Awaiting Judicial Handling

[Our Newspaper Jiangyin 28th Report] Regarding the incident of township head Niu Yusheng killing Xia Li native Sun Pusheng, Sun Guanyin, the father of the deceased, has filed a complaint with the local court. The local procuratorate has scheduled to summon both plaintiffs and defendants Sun Guanyin, Niu Yusheng, and Chen Xingbao, as well as witnesses Huang Enrong, Huang Qichang, Sun Xiaochen (i.e., Yao Cheng), and Sun Fusheng for interrogation on the 31st. This reporter interviewed Magistrate Xu on the 27th. According to him: The county government has ordered Wu Zongyuan, the director of Tang Township, to thoroughly investigate its main issue, whether Sun Pusheng was colluding with bandits or was suspected of it. It will be clear after the report is returned. The reporter asked whether, given the recent bandits in Sun's area, the township head had the right to kill him, and whether there was room for research between killing and intentionally killing. Magistrate Xu replied that since the case had been filed with the judiciary, it should be handled legally, and so on. The conference of all the township heads of the county was held on the same day, and Niu Yusheng also attended. After the reporter met with Township Head Niu, he inquired about the true process of the case. Niu said that before the case was clarified, he was not convenient to express any opinions, but the township office based on the requests submitted by the township residents of this township, such as Du Sheng, Fu Sheng, etc., and the reports from Sun Xida and his wife Lu and Sun Wang, that on July 4, Sun Pusheng brought a gun home, people were uneasy, and Sun Lu, etc., were afraid and wanted to beat her husband Sun Xida. There are official documents to prove this, and third parties in the local area can also come out and testify publicly. The reporter asked that if Sun escaped, had he fired five consecutive shots? Niu replied that there was no fact of firing five shots. In short, since the case is being handled by the judiciary, it will be able to find out the truth. The progress of this case will be reported later.

Moganshan Sanatorium to Reopen on August 1st

[Our Newspaper Moganshan 27th Report] In the summer of the 16th year of the Republic of China, Zhou Bonian had severe hemoptysis and went to Moganshan for recuperation. His condition improved significantly after two months. Zhou believed that Moganshan had a special effect on recuperating from lung diseases, so he invited Li Shizeng and others to initiate the establishment of the Moganshan Sanatorium. Later, the number of people coming to the mountain for recuperation increased day by day, so it was reorganized into a committee system and the wards were rebuilt until the Sino-Japanese War, when it was temporarily closed. Recently, it has been reinvigorated and will resume serving patients on August 1.

The Wolf of Guancun Arrested in Changzhou

[Report from this newspaper on the 27th] Wu Bocai from Guancun, Yixing County, served as the head of the puppet 39th Regiment and a special agent chief during the occupation, along with his father, Wu Jingyuan. They led their troops stationed in Jiyi, extorting and blackmailing people. Many anti-Japanese comrades suffered under their oppression, earning Wu the nickname "The Wolf of Guancun." After the victory, he went into hiding and came to Changzhou, where he opened Ronghecheng Grain Store in Xinhetan outside the West Gate. Recently, Wang Jusheng, a victim from the occupation period, found him and turned him over to the district prosecutor's office for interrogation. The plaintiff, Wang Jusheng, vividly described Wu's crimes of murder and robbery. Wu vehemently denied the accusations. The district prosecutor's office, considering the case involved a major traitor and the seriousness of the charges, approved his transfer to the High Prosecutor's Office for interrogation within days.

Four Criminals in Shenyang, Including Guo Xiushi, Executed by Firing Squad for Disrupting Financial Order

[Central News Agency, Shenyang, 28th] Guo Xiushi, Chen Jilun, Ran Zhongxue, and Tao Junfeng, the main culprits in the case of counterfeiting Central Bank of China Shenyang branch promissory notes, were executed by firing squad here at noon on the 28th. It is reported that Guo and the others were paper merchants and printers who counterfeited Central Bank of China Shenyang branch promissory notes, reaching a huge amount of 1 billion yuan in circulating currency. They were arrested on May 30th. The Northeast Bandit Suppression General Headquarters Military Law Department found that Guo and the others' counterfeiting of promissory notes disrupted the financial order and constituted a crime endangering the state during the period of suppressing the rebellion. Therefore, in accordance with Article 5, Section 1, Item 10 of the Emergency Suppression Regulations, they were sentenced to death.

Policeman Cai Hongsheng Donates Reward Money to Children's Orphanage

Lawyer Jiang Huaisu writes to disclose and commend this action

Dear Editor: I was recently informed by Mr. Cai Hongsheng, formerly a repairman for the city's Defense Corps and currently a policeman at Lin Garden on Hongqiao Road, that at around 3:00 AM on the 23rd of this month, he suddenly heard cries for help from Minglu Garden on Dantian Road, his neighbor. He immediately went to assist with auxiliary policeman Ye Xiao, and saw that Minglu policeman Chen Wanli had been injured in the head by a thief with an iron tiger clamp. Because of his brave assistance, he captured the thief, Huang Guicai, on the spot, and turned him over to the Jihua Branch Bureau for questioning. Afterwards, he received a reward of 20 million yuan from Mr. Zheng Zhangfei, the owner of Mingdui Garden. However, Mr. Cai believes that serving the local community and maintaining security for decades is his duty, and that courageous action and mutual assistance in times of emergency are the spirit that all police officers should have. He feels that accepting Mr. Zheng's reward would be inappropriate and shameful, so he asks to donate it for charitable purposes, in the spirit of helping those in need. I have also heard that the children's orphanage run by Mr. Zhou Zuwang in Caohejing has been teaching and nurturing children well with remarkable results. Mr. Cai, due to his duties, does not have the time to do so himself and has asked me to pass this on for him. Therefore, I am sending Mr. Cai Hongsheng's reward of 20 million yuan to your newspaper to be received and transferred, and I hope that you will disclose the process to commend this action, so as to encourage and inspire others. Sincerely, Jiang Huaisu, July 26th.

Maid Seeking Employment: This newspaper's reader Chen Yulan, a 37-year-old woman from Yingkou, Liaoning Province, graduated from elementary school. She came to Shanghai from her hometown a month ago to look for her brother, but was unsuccessful, leaving her stranded in Shanghai with no food or shelter. She is in a very miserable state. She is currently willing to work as a maid or in a similar position. Communications can be forwarded through this column.

Import Control Committee to Host Press Conference Today to Announce New Policy on Self-Provided Foreign Exchange; Detailed Implementing Rules Have Been Drafted and Will Be Submitted to the Executive Yuan for Approval Today

To increase production and enrich materials, the government authorities have opened up self-provided foreign exchange, so that nationals' funds abroad and overseas Chinese can invest in domestic production businesses such as industry, mining, agriculture, forestry, fisheries, water conservancy, and public transportation. The Import Control Committee (輸管會) has drafted the "Measures for Applying for the Import of Investments in Domestic Production Businesses by Overseas Chinese Capital and Nationals' Funds Abroad," which has been approved by the Executive Yuan. Huo Baoshu, the chairman of the Import Control Committee, is scheduled to hold a press conference at 4:00 PM today on the fourth floor of the Bank of China Building to announce this new policy and implement it. It is said that the committee is currently drafting detailed implementing rules for the new measures. Yesterday, Chairman Huo was busy discussing various technical issues with relevant parties, so that they could be released at the press conference today.

Another report: To accelerate the implementation of these measures, the Import Control Committee has appointed Huang Qinghua, Director of the Non-Quota Examination Department; Shen Zouting, Director of the Quota Allocation Department; Chen Junren, Director of the Promotion Department; and Fang Yuanxian, Director of the Secretariat, to form a small committee responsible for designing detailed implementing rules. It is reported that the detailed rules have been drafted and will be submitted to the Executive Yuan for approval today. It is said that the detailed implementing rules specify the types of materials that can be imported. It is reported that in addition to the production equipment in Appendix (1), the industrial raw materials in Appendix (2) and the parts in Appendix (3) can also be applied for import. However, the Import Control Committee will still closely monitor the use of imported materials. As for the handling of overseas Chinese capital imports, another small committee will be set up to be responsible. (The articles on the measures for applying for the import of investments in domestic production businesses by overseas Chinese capital and nationals' funds abroad can be found on the second page.)

Strong Demand for Rice Drives Prices Up; Flour, Grain, Oilcakes Also Rise in Unison

The rice market rose again. The market close on the previous day had already shifted to a firm trend, so the opening yesterday morning was also strong. Rice shops had very good demand, because credit was loose and sales were active. White japonica rice and thin japonica rice in the northern market were both 37 million yuan, while some high-quality japonica rice was priced at 40 million yuan. New japonica rice from Pudong continued to be offered in the southern market, priced at 38 million yuan. Brown rice mills also had good demand, with prices rising by 2.5 million yuan each. However, the market softened slightly at the close because demand had been met. Yesterday's arrivals were 4,485 piculs.

Flour continued to rise, due to loose credit, rising rice prices, and expectations of higher prices. Retailers absorbed supplies and actual sales were also strong. Old Che flour opened at 11.8 million yuan, once reaching 12 million yuan, but closed slightly lower at 11.5 million yuan, a rise of 500,000 yuan. Bingship Flour rose by 700,000 yuan to 10.7 million yuan. Hongfeng and Jiancheng were both at 10.5 million yuan. Unhulled wheat rose by 450,000 yuan. Large bags of bran were 8.25 million yuan.

Miscellaneous grains rose in unison. With the easing of credit, demand from customers strengthened, and vendors were even more insistent on raising prices. Soybeans rose by 1 million yuan. Corn, broad beans, and northern sales were sluggish, with only a slight increase of 500,000 yuan. Barley rose by 1 million yuan. Broad beans increased by 500,000 yuan. Red sorghum rose by 1 million yuan. Sesame seeds rose by 2 million yuan. Shelled peanuts had strong demand from Guangdong merchants, rising by 4 million yuan.

Cooking Oil

Continued to rise. With the loosening of credit, all commodities rose, and expectations were strong. Vendors held firm. However, soybean oil rose only slightly yesterday because it had already risen on the previous day. Factory soybean oil opened at 74 million yuan and closed at 73 million yuan, a slight increase of 1 million yuan. The same was true for raw rapeseed oil. Raw oil rose by 5 million yuan. Jiton raw oil was 95 million yuan. Sesame oil from small mills rose the most, increasing by 8 million yuan. Soybean cakes continued to rise, increasing by 400,000 to 500,000 yuan.

Flat Water Tea Exports Sluggish

Flat water green tea has always been sold mostly to America, but in recent years, since Japanese tea has been selling cheaply and extensively, the demand for this tea is not as urgent as before. Furthermore, the price offered is always an attempt to suppress prices. As such, it seems that Chinese tea in America has gradually lost its importance. At present, the only outlet for Chinese tea is the Mediterranean coast of Europe, but recently the price offered is also very harsh. Exporters in the city have repeatedly telegraphed to request a price increase, but they have not been able to get it. As a result, the tea market for foreign merchants has been greatly diminished. Any trades that have been made are only for waiting for shipment. As for the trend, the sellers are holding firm and not discouraged, and the future looks like it will rise. As for domestic tea, the market continues steadily with very few changes.

Unclaimed Allied Bonds to be Surrendered to National Treasury for Verification and Cancellation

[Report from this newspaper] A message from the National Treasury Bureau of the Central Bank of China: the Allied bonds for the 31st, 32nd, and 33rd years of the Republic have already been fully subscribed. The Ministry of Finance previously stipulated that those who had not yet exchanged their bonds had until the end of March of this year to complete the exchange. If they failed to do so, they would be considered to have donated to the state and would be surrendered to the treasury for verification and cancellation. Now that the deadline has passed, any overdue exchanges will be handled in accordance with the regulations, unless there are special circumstances that have been approved by the Ministry.

Meeting Held Yesterday on Distributing Relief Supplies for Fisheries in Seven Provinces

[Report from this newspaper] The opening ceremony of the meeting on the distribution of relief supplies for fisheries in seven provinces was held yesterday (28th) at 9:00 AM at the Eight Immortals Bridge Youth Association. Attending were representatives from the Ministry of Agriculture and Forestry, the Ministry of Transportation, the Ministry of Social Affairs, the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, and the city government, as well as representatives from the relevant authorities and fishery organizations of the seven provinces of Jiangsu and Zhejiang, the cities of Shanghai and Tianjin, and representatives from the expert committees and the custody committee. Approximately 80 people were present. The meeting was presided over by Pan Xulun, acting chairman of the Relief Committee, who reported on the preparations for the meeting. Representatives from the various ministries then gave speeches. Xie Chengping, Vice Minister of Agriculture and Forestry, and Cao Peizi, Director of the Ministry of Social Affairs, expressed their hope that the meeting would achieve satisfactory results, so that the fishery supplies could be quickly distributed to the coastal provinces and benefit the fishermen. Wei Weiheng, a representative from the Ministry of Transportation, stated that some of the lumber among the fishery supplies was not suitable for shipbuilding and hoped to sell it to the Ministry of Transportation for use as bridge-building materials. The proceeds would be distributed to the provinces to build wooden boats, so that "the materials would be used properly." Subsequently, Ouyang Duan, Director of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, and Li Zhuomin, Executive Member of the Custody Committee, gave speeches, expressing their high expectations for the meeting and hoping that the supplies could reach the hands of the fishermen directly. Finally, Gu Bingyuan, representing Mayor Wu, welcomed the representatives from various places to Shanghai to attend the fishery meeting.

After the opening ceremony, a group photo was taken at 10:30 AM, and at 11:30 AM, the representatives went to the Fishery Administration Office to visit.

At 3:00 PM in the afternoon, the first general meeting was held. The chairman read aloud the origin of the "Plan for the Use of Fishery Supplies in the Seven Regions of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Fujian, etc." and reported on the resolutions regarding the distribution plan of the fishery supplies. Subsequently, the Custody Committee reported on the general situation of the fishery timber and vessel materials, and the Fishery Administration Office reported on the storage situation of the fishery supplies. Finally, the meeting passed the rules of procedure and the list of the three review groups for "Ship Construction," "Distribution Ratio," and "Material Allocation." Review meetings will be held on the 29th in the morning and afternoon. A general meeting will be held on the 30th to discuss the results of the review by the various groups.

Alkali Industry Prospects Optimistic; Taiwan Province Prepares to Increase Production

The prospects for the alkali industry in our country are extremely optimistic. According to surveys, the total amount of caustic soda required by various industries is more than 7,800 tons per quarter. The current production of all domestic manufacturers using the electrolytic method is more than 3,300 tons per quarter. In addition, about 1,700 tons of caustic soda are produced from soda ash and lime per quarter. The shortfall is about 2,800 tons. Now, the Taiwan Alkali Industry Company has prepared a plan to increase production. By the end of this year, the quarterly output can reach 3,600 tons. (Currently, it is only 1,500 tons per quarter.) If other electrochemical plants can further increase power and increase production, coupled with the caustic soda made from soda ash and lime, then the caustic soda problem in our country can be self-sufficient. According to the results of the on-site investigation by the Industry and Commerce Guidance Office, the current production and sales of caustic soda are as follows: (1) The national quarterly output totals 10,998,414 pounds. (2) The national quarterly demand of various industries: the Shanghai area requires 17,199,725 pounds, the Hankou area requires 1,104,840 pounds, the Changsha area requires 137,620 pounds, the Nanchang area requires 58,420 pounds, the Hengyang area requires 7,920 pounds, the Kaifeng area requires 9,900 pounds, and the Wuchang area requires 80,190 pounds, totaling 18,598,615 pounds.

Prices of Gold Ornaments Must be Reported to the Authorities for Record After Determination

New Silversmiths Not Allowed to be Established

The Social Affairs Bureau, in accordance with last week's municipal meeting, has decided on measures for the gold jewelry business in the city. Yesterday, it specially notified the silversmiths' trade association that after the prices of gold jewelry transactions are determined by the trade association, in addition to reporting to the Social Affairs Bureau for record, they must also be reported to the Police Bureau and the Gold Control Bureau for record. Regarding the question of whether new silversmiths will be allowed to be established in the city in the future, according to the relevant department of the Social Affairs Bureau, with the exception of the 185 that have already been approved, in accordance with Article 4 of the "Measures for the Administration of Silversmiths' Collection, Redemption, and Manufacture of Gold Jewelry" amended and promulgated by the Ministry of Finance on December 31 of last year, they are not allowed to be established.

Yesterday's cotton yarn market conditions: due to the Spinning and Construction Company raising the price by 200 million yuan, morale suddenly became excited. Yesterday's cotton cloth market conditions: due to the easing of credit and remittances from other ports to Shanghai, the funds of merchants were abundant, northern merchants were actively purchasing, and there was news that external prices were about to move again, making people feel even more confident. 12-pound Dragon Head fine cloth rose by 4.3 million yuan immediately after opening. However, because the previous day's floating price was too high, the market price suddenly fell by 1.2 million yuan. At this time, the industry was secretly absorbing supplies very strongly. After 10:30, the market atmosphere became even more brisk, and bids to buy at 50 million yuan were made, but no transactions were made. 14th World Olympic Games to Open in London Today with 61 Nations and Over 6,000 Athletes Participating in 17 Sports, Displaying an Unprecedented Spectacle

[Our Report] The 14th Olympic World Games, the first World Games after the war, will hold a grand opening ceremony at 4:00 PM today (July 29th) at the Wembley Empire Stadium in London. King George VI of England will personally attend to declare the opening of the 14th World Games. A total of 61 countries are participating in this session, with more than 6,100 athletes competing in 17 sports. The spectacle will set a new record never seen before in World Games history. The official competition will begin tomorrow and end on August 14th, lasting a total of two weeks, with Sundays as rest days. Unfortunately, three countries with outstanding athletes were unable to participate this session. The Soviet Union did not accept the invitation, while Germany and Japan were not qualified to participate. Since the Berlin World Games, more than ten years have passed, and athletes from various countries have not had the chance to show their skills in the World Games. Many new world records will likely be set this session. Among the various competitions this session, the track and field events are the most attention-grabbing, with representative athletes from 59 countries participating. Our country, in this difficult time, also has a delegation of thirty to forty athletes participating. The number of athletes in track and field, swimming, and cycling is relatively small, but the two football and basketball teams hope to have a good performance in the World Games, even if they cannot achieve any victories.

[Agence France-Presse, London, July 27th] The current heatwave sweeping through England is causing headaches for athletes and coaches from various countries. The performance of Nordic athletes in training seems to have been greatly affected by the intense heat, while South American, South African, and black athletes are happy and at ease.

Wang Zhengting Broadcasts in England on the Mission of the World Games and the Purpose of China's Participation

[Central News Agency, London, July 28th] Wang Zhengting, the general leader of our World Games delegation, stated in a broadcast speech on the London National Broadcasting Corporation today that the 14th World Games, with the participation of over 5,000 representatives from 61 countries, is indeed an effective institution for promoting international understanding and cooperation, which are indispensable for world peace. While reporting on the situation of the World Games to our country in Mandarin on the British National Broadcasting Corporation, Wang expressed his deep gratitude for the warm reception of our delegation by the United Kingdom, and also highly praised the United Kingdom for its efforts to make this grand event a success despite extreme financial and economic difficulties. Wang stated that our country's delegation attending the World Games is not too interested in winning medals, but rather wants to observe the sportsmanship of other countries and study the advanced techniques and organization of the sports world in other countries. He also mentioned the most important steps for our country to improve sports, train better sports instructors, and build more sports fields.

The Origin of the Olympic Games and the Revival of Modern World Games

[Special Feature by Our Newspaper] The origin and cause of the Olympic Games have long been lost to history. Judging from the fact that Iphitos in 776 BC was called the "reviver" of the Olympics, the founding of the Olympics dates back more than 2,700 years.

The Olympic Games, since Iphitos restarted it, lasted for thirteen centuries. In 394 AD, the host, Roman King Theodosius, considering the declining morality of the competitors, who often resorted to various despicable means to win the championship, believed that the original spirit of promoting sports and connecting emotions had been completely lost. Therefore, he ordered a permanent ban on the holding of the Olympics. Soon, the statue of Zeus, the king of the Greek gods, was also burned, and the Olympics was suspended for more than 1,500 years.

Revival of the Modern Olympic Games

The revival of the modern Olympic Games, becoming a global event held every four years, must be attributed to Sir Coubertin, a French soldier and scholar. From the army, the knight observed that a sound physique could only come from sports training. Furthermore, from the history of Greece, he studied that the decline of ancient countries was also greatly related to the Olympics. Thus, he engaged in launching a grand World Games plan, hoping that the World Games could connect the cultures of various countries, eliminate the barriers between various ethnic groups, thereby eliminating world war and achieving lasting peace.

In 1893, the knight launched the first step of the plan, sending letters in his private capacity to sports leaders of various countries, suggesting a meeting in Paris the following year to discuss methods for the resumption of the Olympics. As a result of the meeting, it was unanimously passed to hold the first modern World Games in 1896, and it was stipulated that it would be held every four years thereafter.

The First Session Held in Athens

The first World Games were held in Athens, the capital of Greece, to commemorate the ancient Olympics. Thanks to the donation of a nobleman, a large marble stadium, which was already hailed as magnificent and majestic at the time, was built in this ancient cultural capital.

After a series of arduous preparations, the modern Olympics finally opened. Everything was just beginning, and only twelve units participated in the competition. The events were also simple and basic, but they had already aroused the attention of enlightened people around the world, opening up a broad path for the subsequent World Games.

After that, the second, third, fourth, and fifth sessions were held every four years in Paris, St. Louis, London, and Stockholm, respectively. Although the third session had only eight units participating due to the long distance and the ongoing Russo-Japanese War, with a turbulent situation, the World Games were indeed progressing towards perfection, one session better than the previous.

European War Destroys the World Games

Sir Coubertin's ideal was shattered. In 1916, the Olympics not only failed to eliminate war, but was burned down by war. The sixth session was thus aborted.

In 1920, the seventh session was held in the capital of Belgium, which suffered the most from the ravages of the god of war during the Great War. Twenty-five units participated, with 117 events, breaking the records of the previous sessions.

In 1924, Paris hosted the Games for the second time, with forty-five countries participating, and the events gradually became more complete.

The ninth World Games were held in Amsterdam, the capital of the Netherlands. Four thousand athletes from forty-three countries participated in the competition. The ninth session made a major and successful attempt, establishing women's track and field events for the first time.

Our Country's Historic Attempt

In 1932, in the midst of the peak of the world economic crisis, the tenth session was held in Los Angeles. Although due to economic reasons, the number of athletes sent by various countries was far smaller than in previous sessions, the quality was far superior to any previous session. Sixteen world records and twenty-five conference records were broken in this gathering of heroes. Our country also made a historic attempt, sending Liu Changchun, an athlete, for the first time. Although he failed due to natural and acquired reasons, it also renewed the eyes of foreigners and corrected many absurd imaginations of foreigners about China in terms of international perception.

After the first World War, Germany, which became increasingly powerful, hosted the eleventh session in 1936. The scientific mind and fighting spirit of the Germans made this session unprecedented. The largest sports stadium and the most well-equipped World Games Village impressed athletes from fifty-one countries and thousands of tourists from all over the world. It is regrettable that this global conference has reached its peak in terms of material resources, but the spiritual gains are pitifully scarce. The mad war drove away the god of peace again, and the twelfth and thirteenth sessions were aborted in the womb.

The first session after the war has been scheduled to open in London today. In fact, this session is only the twelfth, but from 1896, it has been the fourteenth "Olympiad" (Olmpiad in Greek, originally meaning a four-year period). (Xin)

Free Talk

Snippets of New Conversations (In Nanjing)

— Bai Yong

The electricity is cut off one day out of every three. Tonight, it is again a world of darkness. Dark clouds cover the sky, and even the expected moon offers no light. The indoor temperature is a hundred degrees. Everyone is cooling off in the courtyard. Although there isn't much of a breeze to be found, at least the air is stirring a bit. Unfortunately, the rain is coming again, so we have no choice but to trim the candle by the west window. The price of each "Monk's Cap" brand candle has reached 500,000, but there's no other option.

Coincidentally, guests arrived, perfectly fitting the ancient saying of trimming candles and talking in the night rain. The two guests could be called "old friends" or "new friends." As for the former, we were all poor fellow villagers to begin with, and our conversations have something in common. As for the latter, they have already leaped from being poor to becoming "bosses," which puts them in a different category from me, this white-haired scholar who will grow old under the window. However, listening to their "wild tales" is still a source of historical material, "therefore, I record them."

Guest A: "Today, pork is 900,000, and a 'jin' (catty) is only fifteen taels. But it's not fixed. At Shuixi Gate, it sells for 800,000, at Caixia Street it's 640,000, and at Xinqiao it's 720,000. Look, what counts as the standard! The price of soybean sprouts is completely different: 120,000, 100,000, and even 150,000!"

Me: "Let's not talk about this. I heard you've been making a lot of money recently. What business are you doing exactly?"

Guest B: "Don't you know? He's been trafficking in livestock. The last time it was more than 3 billion!"

Me: "Oh? How does that work?"

B (smiling at A): "There was a major flood in Jiangbei this year, and the situation in the Suxian area is even worse. Added to that is the fighting. Livestock are all being sold at low prices. A horse costs no more than 50 million. You can easily earn over 100 million in Nanjing. The villagers are easy to deceive. They don't necessarily pay in cash. After the purchase is settled, they pay a hundred or two upfront, and the rest is paid with promissory notes. Selling on credit for ten days or half a month is nothing. With a quick turnaround, you can make money hand over fist."

A (uneasy, but also self-satisfied): "Don't listen to his nonsense. He stockpiled gasoline half a month ago, and now he's already doubled his profit. Today, he asked me to buy used oil drums. Last week, a drum was 400,000, but in the last few days, it's risen to 220,000, even those made from tin can scraps. Do you know why? Public school employees are allocated oil, and everyone has to buy containers to collect it, so there's been a big fluctuation in the market. It's true, even broken tiles have their day!"

Me: "I never thought that you, who used to be in the used book business and looked down on gold and silver, would be getting involved in this now?"

B: "Can books still be sold? A ream of newsprint costs over 5,000, and a single sheet sells for up to 200,000. Any old book costs over a million. Even if people have money, who would buy these things? Used books are even worse. Firstly, no one reads them, and secondly, the prices don't go up. Look, those used bookstores in Zhuangyuanjing are all selling by weight. The shelves are full of Feng Yuqi novels and patriotic songs. We, who talk about Song and Yuan editions, don't even bother! Several new bookstores from Beiping came to Jiangnan hoping to strike it rich, but they were all disappointed. Those who are willing to use their brains don't sell new books and instead switch back to stationery. Look, isn't a Parker fountain pen equivalent to US dollars? What we're doing is nothing!"

I was stunned, unsure how to respond.

Just then, B finished a cigarette and threw the remaining half-smoked butt on the ground: "Don't look down on this cigarette butt. It's worth a thousand or so. A house used to cost that much, and now it's lightly discarded!"

Everyone burst out laughing.

The rain stopped, and the two figures in plaid cotton disappeared into the shadows.

As I listened to the rain, I pondered this month's cost of living index, wondering how many times it should be multiplied.

Generally, when Western men encounter women on the street, they naturally remove their hats as a sign of respect. Over time, everyone has come to see this as a matter of habit, rarely thinking about the underlying meaning of respecting the opposite sex. In fact, this custom of removing hats to women evolved from an ancient law, the main purpose of which was to force "all inferiors to remove their head coverings before superiors as a sign of respect."

This law can be traced back even earlier to the custom of stripping prisoners of war of their clothing. In ancient times, the Assyrians stripped all prisoners of war of their clothes, showing their complete subjugation. Therefore, nudity was regarded as a form of worship. Even now, the custom of nudity to show respect for "superiors" still exists in some primitive tribal peoples.

As Westerners gradually became more civilized, this custom was slightly modified in form and passed down. In the age of the samurai, warriors were fully armored when they appeared in public. However, when friendly warriors met, they would remove their helmets to show recognition and respect. When these warriors encountered a lady, they would completely remove their armor. They did so to show respect or to reveal their true selves. In any case, there is no doubt that the warriors unknowingly passed on the habit of "inferiors" respecting "superiors" to later generations.

When the samurai system declined, men changed to wearing hats, and they retained the samurai custom of removing helmets for women.

Members of the Religious Society of Friends (Quakers) were somewhat averse to this custom and refused to remove their hats to women. Because they believed that they only had one "superior," that is, God.

Three Excellent Paintings with Inscriptions

— Zhang Yiqu

Discussing objects and satirizing the times, the artistic conception is novel,

The people's spirit is not inferior to that of the poet;

A few strokes of the brush, more mellow than wine,

Begging to be drunk in West Lake every spring. (The teacher has lived by West Lake for nearly three years.)

Inscription on Yu Shaosong's Ink Bamboo

Like Su Dongpo's elegant bamboo branches,

The clustered growth, the slender roots, the shadows, are irregular;

The dripping drunken ink is just like you,

Still remembering the time we drank together that year. (In Longyou in 1927, I drank with the teacher all night.)

Inscription on Feng Chaoran's Landscape Painting

Mountains and waters, a wild family's home,

The artistic conception of the painting and the poetic sentiment grow richer with age;

Painting to the point of a tranquil, leisure place,

A crescent moon accompanies plum blossoms.

According to Washington-based reporter Robert Allen, US Secretary of State Marshall can truly be said to be a "man of few meals and many tasks." There are now as many as 74 diplomatic missions stationed in Washington, breaking all previous records, but Marshall often only eats very casually at his desk in the office, eating only an apple and a bottle of milk for lunch. (Mei)

Random Thoughts on Jing'an Temple

— Chen Zuogao

Jing'an Temple was a famous place for escaping the heat and spending the summer in the late Qing Dynasty. Every summer, tourists came in droves. As the sun set, groups of people would arrive with fans and light shirts. Some brought their families, some brought their concubines. Decorated carriages turned and jade wheels rolled. Even late at night, among the sounds of pines and bamboos, there were still hairpins and earrings left behind. Today, there is an ancient well in front of the temple, located next to a streetcar station, called the Sixth Spring Under Heaven. During the Guangxu period of the Qing Dynasty, a tea house was built on top of it. Tang Jingsong, the famous minister of the Sino-French War, once went to the temple with the Chaozhou scholar Xiao Daonong to see the ancient well. The spring water seemed to be boiling, which was the case every year. They went upstairs for tea cakes. "Women surrounded the seats, charming and lovely, but could not endure the cold and returned." See Tang's "Please Enlist" Diary, entry for October 23rd of the Guangxu 12th year.

Shen Garden was located next to the temple. Huang Xietong's "Record of Dreams in Songnan" described the place as having painted beams and pearl curtains, rising and falling with the morning and evening, showing the grandeur of the buildings and the elegance of the furnishings. When tired of walking, one could lean on the carved railing and sip bitter tea. A fresh breeze would blow away all worldly worries. Sometimes, flower branches would reach out from across the seat, beckoning to people. The sound of hairpins and the shadows of ornaments seemed to be in the curtain, and one would often recite Yuan Xiang's "Drunk, I hear the flowers rising; waking, I hear the orioles," lingering and unable to leave. Downstairs, there were several billiard tables where one could gamble under the moonlight. Western food was also available, but guests had to order in advance to avoid being caught unprepared. It is said that while drinking tea, there were also singers performing to add to the fun. A Shanghai ballad said, "With an appointment at Shen Garden to enjoy tea, hastily ascending the seat to play the pipa. After the song ends, she goes down to the singing building, and the horse-drawn carriages linger at the door." This probably refers to this.

Thirty-two years ago, when I was free on holidays, I would come with old scholars from Zhejiang to the temple to chat over tea. Forerunners such as Gao Yehou and Ding Fuzhi also attended. I occasionally sat at the end of the table, enjoying the eloquent conversations. Thinking back to the temple in those days, flowers were dense, brocade layers, forever soft dust fragrant, and various other beauties filled it. But now the temple grounds are narrower, the scenery is completely different, the surrounding buildings are crowded together, and vehicles converge, just like what Bao Mingyuan called "four-way intersections." Alas, in this noisy city, who would still see it as a scenic spot! Reflecting on the past and thinking about the present, how can one not feel a sense of vicissitudes?
